    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_228772436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228772436" />
    <a title="Arun Divakar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar"><img alt="Arun Divakar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228772436?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arun Divakar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arun Divakar" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar">Arun Divakar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228772436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15674134347159127561">Espionage stories set during the premise of the cold war are probably the most alluring of all backdrops that thriller writers can think of. Two of the world's super powers while in all external appearances behaved like bosom buddies hid daggers beneath their smiles and behind closed rooms plotted how to outwit each other. While this was going on the world would have lived in perennial trepidation of an impending holocaust. But then in 1991, the USSR vanished and the soviet bloc suddenly ceased </span>
  <span id="freeText15674134347159127561" style="display:none">Espionage stories set during the premise of the cold war are probably the most alluring of all backdrops that thriller writers can think of. Two of the world's super powers while in all external appearances behaved like bosom buddies hid daggers beneath their smiles and behind closed rooms plotted how to outwit each other. While this was going on the world would have lived in perennial trepidation of an impending holocaust. But then in 1991, the USSR vanished and the soviet bloc suddenly ceased to exist. As easy as it sounds, the threat disappeared &amp; the Americans moved on to get involved in other bigger messes. Interesting isn't it ? Many authors seem to think so too judging by the number of spy thrillers out there &amp; I admit to the fact that I am a sucker for them !<br /><br />Simply put, the plot line is : <i>Invasion of the body snatchers meets cloak &amp; dagger espionage </i>. The KGB on the path to world domination through a massive intelligence offensive and the Americans out to stop them is what it is all about. The first 100 pages showed a lot of promise in this plot and then as suddenly as it had appeared, the promise disappeared. DeMille puts a lot of focus on Russia during the Cold War era and to his credit I must say that the plot covers some of the pros and the cons of this enigmatic landscape. The characters are thoroughly one dimensional and forgettable with the good being startlingly brilliant shades of white and evil being hey-who-turned-out-the-lights black. For a novel which some one termed as a gem in cold war literature, this had some of the mushiest romantic scenes I have ever read. Bleh !<br /><br />The best parts are the dialog between the characters for Demille writes some of the wittiest verbal banter which alternates between the cheeky to the chuckle out loud kind of humor. I would recommend this as an entertainer,akin to the kind of movies Roland Emmerich makes (minus the explosions that is !).</span>
  <a data-text-id="15674134347159127561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_590477227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590477227" />
    <a title="R.L. Anderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7573688-r-l-anderson"><img alt="R.L. Anderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335389850p2/7573688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/590477227?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.L. Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.L. Anderson" href="/user/show/7573688-r-l-anderson">R.L. Anderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590477227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6983099491673139242">One of the best Cold War thrillers ever! A real page turner that I couldn't put down. Also very educational, as it describes details of the lives of American diplomats working in a US embassy in a hostile (at the time) nation, the old Soviet Union. One little detail that sticks in my mind is the mention that US diplomats are some of the most patriotic Americans you could ever hope to meet--but yet they are just not "into" the popular culture. Hmmmmm.... That sounds strange, doesn't it? Well--the</span>
  <span id="freeText6983099491673139242" style="display:none">One of the best Cold War thrillers ever! A real page turner that I couldn't put down. Also very educational, as it describes details of the lives of American diplomats working in a US embassy in a hostile (at the time) nation, the old Soviet Union. One little detail that sticks in my mind is the mention that US diplomats are some of the most patriotic Americans you could ever hope to meet--but yet they are just not "into" the popular culture. Hmmmmm.... That sounds strange, doesn't it? Well--the more thought I gave to it, the more I realized that I am very much that way myself!!! Guess I'd make a good member of the Diplomatic Corps. This is an excellent book and one of many I've read that gradually steered me away from sci fi, which I had been a big fan of as a kid, and into the mystery genre. I am now writing mysteries, myself, Ranch Park, It's A Place For Trees, and Viking It Is--although mine are of a much more tame domestic nature, as I don't have the knowledge and experience in international affairs to be able to write an international thriller such as this. Nelson DeMille shows that he is truly an expert in this field. Maybe I will be someday when I have the opportunity to do more traveling. The Charm School comes highly recommended by this mystery author of a very different kind of mystery. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6983099491673139242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3aEuLam3MgxQB+74NpZma8J7Hsepie3/saYC3cetFi9+3l7BPzT1KNRmHeBXsZKIv/QfJmO/pI5LkWwg6OvpFg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MUG6iF0Jgsvq2ns73EGdhEBuHBJjkt/a1j6KRiFVqISSPspky4pF7267iCO9ZmlnPeEd86mklqssCeS7DhNXvQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">About Nelson DeMille</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1498066748p3/1238.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">Nelson DeMille

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16088706922932913878">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br/><br/>DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United S</span>
  <span id="freeText16088706922932913878" style="display:none">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69). He saw action in Vietnam as an infantry platoon leader with the First Cavalry Division and was decorated with the Air Medal, Bronze Star, and the Vietnamese Cross of Gallantry.<br /><br />After his discharge, DeMille returned to Hofstra University where he received his bachelor’s degree in Political Science and History. He has three children, Lauren, Alexander, and James, and resides on Long Island.<br /><br />DeMille's first major novel was By the Rivers of Babylon, published in 1978, and is still in print as are all his succeeding novels. He is a member of American Mensa, The Authors Guild, and is past president of the Mystery Writers of America. He is also a member of International Thriller Writers and was chosen as ThrillerMaster of the Year 2015. He holds three honorary doctorates: Doctor of Humane Letters from Hofstra University, Doctor of Literature from Long Island University, and Doctor of Humane Letters from Dowling College.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is the author of: By the Rivers of Babylon, Cathedral, The Talbot Odyssey, Word of Honor, The Charm School, The Gold Coast, The General's Daughter, Spencerville, Plum Island, The Lion's Game, Up Country, Night Fall, Wild Fire, The Gate House, The Lion, The Panther, The Quest, Radiant Angel, The Cuban Affair and The Deserter. He also co-authored Mayday with Thomas Block and has contributed short stories to anthologies, and book reviews and articles to magazines and newspapers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16088706922932913878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
